## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: The task involves acceleration (dv/dt) as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, describing a non-linear harmonic oscillator. This falls within classical nonlinear dynamics, where Newton's second law yields a second-order ODE, often with nonlinear restoring forces, damping, or driving terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring force proportional to displacement; corresponds to simple harmonic motion)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinearity in restoring force, hardening/softening spring)
- Pendulum restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force characteristic of a simple pendulum)
- van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v + c2 * x (nonlinear damping producing self-sustained limit-cycle oscillations)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * x (damping with cubic velocity term, another self-oscillator)
- Quadratic drag oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (damping proportional to square of velocity; conservative + drag)
- Forced oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external harmonic driving force)
- Parametric excitation: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (stiffness modulated periodically in time, as in Mathieu's equation)
- Nonlinear spring with softening: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (restoring force that saturates or weakens at large displacements)
- General polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v**3 + c4 * x**2 * v + c5 * x * v**2 (Taylor expansion of a general second-order nonlinear ODE)
- Coulomb friction oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (smooth approximation of dry, sliding friction)
- Toda oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (exp(c1 * x) - 1) (exponential interaction potential, exhibits soliton solutions)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative dynamics → dv_dt depends solely on x (position), with no explicit v or t dependence, implying energy conservation.
- Nonlinear restoring force → acceleration contains odd powers of x (x, x^3, ...) or trigonometric functions of x (sin, tanh), leading to amplitude-dependent period.
- Velocity-dependent damping → terms like v, v^3, v*|v|, or sign(v) indicate energy dissipation or friction.
- Limit cycle behavior → damping coefficient changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (1 - c*x^2) multiplying v, giving negative damping at small amplitude and positive at large.
- External forcing → explicit harmonic functions of time t that do not involve x or v represent an external drive.
- Parametric resonance → time-periodic coefficients multiplying x, e.g., x * cos(t), indicating modulation of system parameters.
- Asymmetric potential → presence of even powers of x (x^2) or mixed parity terms suggests a potential without inversion symmetry.
- Non-analytic friction → terms like sign(v), tanh(c*v) model dry friction; v*abs(v) models quadratic (hydraulic) drag.
- Nonlinear damping with position coupling → terms like x*v or x^2*v describe damping that depends on the oscillator's position.
- Amplitude-frequency coupling → cubic or higher odd-power restoring terms (x^3, x^5) cause the oscillation period to change with amplitude.
